Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Here is the translation:
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After you apply the two inflamed veins so that the heart is perceived from the other side, and then draw fire cautery, and thus you will have four. And if you see, if you cauterize the entire cautery to four veins.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has obtained purification by long tension, and this is more than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire cautery is not suitable for hydropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you do four cauteries around the belly, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the spleen, and two behind the back above the spine, and one on the piss; and let the cauteries be very close to the width of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, let the cautery be opened for a short time, and do not leave the treatment of the patient's ailment after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the four intentions will be together with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the club-like shape that we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of yellow watery fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and anular; and hold your hand with the cauterizing iron without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not insert it too deeply, lest you would push back the yellow watery fluid, and let the cauterizing iron be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit. de la menoison	of the menorhea
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	Here is the translation:

de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, one or more, and are old and are of large cold and moist corrupt humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, if you make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, which is all divided below in a triangle, and one cauterization below the navel two fingers; and if you think that the stomach is refrigerated, and the food does not digest, and you see the face inflating, then you make one great cauterization on the stomach, as it has been said before, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen with all the clavicle cauterizations; and let the cauterization be open for a long time.

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness that is named "thelul"

When you burn the fleshiness called "thelul", if you heat the cautery that seems appropriate, and then apply it thoroughly to the burned "thelul"; and hold your hand so the cauteries reach the base of the vein, where the blood flows freely; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of "thelul", if you cauterialize each one as we have said; after the treatment of useful remedies, they will be healthy; and if you apply a large cautery to the affected area, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the pain of a high temperature, which we will describe in its place, then comes such an illness that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes, and it is wrapped and casts putrid and corrupted moisture, if you want to prove all of a subtle tent, and beware that you know all of the tent how deep it has.

se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, beware of these limbs, and do not make those false passages in a charnel house, and think that it is not a permanent injury; after healing the limb as long as it is sound, and if the limbs are healthy, and the materials are removed from the tension, then know that the limb is entirely sound; and if the materials are not removed, know that the limb is troubled, and corrupts the bone at the font; and thus one of those things that we will direct in its limb.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys

de la marris	of the marrow

de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the joints of the department are twisted, so it is necessary to cautery the patient on the hip joint with a .i. cautery similar to a circle, and mark in front of the joint around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those with which one has cautered the stomach.

de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the ankle

Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And it is the manner in which one does on the thigh, when the pain holds in the thigh, and does not reach as far as the knee nor as far as the leg.

Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction. de la dolor dou dos	from the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from a fall or percussion or by excessive evacuation, or by expansion of cold matter, none of these appearances is worth cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.

de la dolor des jointes	from the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints comes from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes on foot, which the physician properly calls "podagra", and when it is from cold cause and treatments with medicines cannot cure it, if it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the mount of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-like according to this method.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick on the surface of the foot, you should make a complete cautery at every point that one calls a "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come near the knees and other joints, and this happens often, you should make a cautery on each knee, three or four cauteries on each part, with a complete olive-tree cautery; and if you have more skill, do more, but do not hold your hand firmly unless the space of the heart is prepared.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist and two lines; and if there remains a point of pain in both, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the wrists or just to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good government for the patient and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good government for him and you purge bad blood, he will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	about the treatment of swelling
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes from anger, and the blood descends to the intestines and it's new, then you should understand that when you want to cure the wound, you must not neglect that day; and he uses things that loosen the belly, so that the fiens descend from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm as long as the intestine is repaired, and put it in your two hands, and sign underneath the rupture on the bone of the finger, and at all a sign that would be similar to half a circle above the body; then apply the cautery in the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until he is pale and feels sensations.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the boules to their place; and you hold his hand so that they do not return back; and work well on the hips of the patient, and put under him a cushion and a strap on the hips, and another on the pis who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign all over his hand, and the right vein and the vein as much as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again until you come to the bone; and be subtly careful that the bouil does not jump when you make the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and so that by this the patients do not die, or other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your operations are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and for great people as great according to their measure; after three days cure the wound with the cautery of borax so that the inflammation be removed; after curing other wounds so that they be healthy, and let the patient lie forty days on his back so that the wound be well healed; and it is necessary that their bandages be loosened slowly, so that the boils do not burst when they prepare to get up from their chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when they want to get up, a well-made poultice is applied to them, and they are spared for another forty days; and let them have good rest, so that they work little and beware of too great repletion of drinking and eating, and of too high feasting; and when they follow this teaching, they will be entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will describe hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When roots grow into other bellies and are conjoined, and you see that they do not increase anymore, then make I the fire cautery of two fires burning according to their quantity, and be the third fire of the cauterizer; after the treatment according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one must cauterize at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the level of the notch and make a line according to the width above the root, and another below, and hold your hand in all the fire of the cauterizing instrument.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more moderate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in any member (or limb)
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to a member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no value, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsions and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if he is healthy enough for the first cautery, it's good; if not, begin another cautery on that one, because such is the custom that it should be moved to the member that is closest, so it is necessary that you perform the cauteries until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The messengers are often helped by cautery with great aid, and especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You cannot see the cautery site, take care that the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not descend nor delay, and you fear that the corruption will not spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one on the new head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the horns, and one behind on the temple; and leave so much space with your hand that the cauteries come just to the bone, and until the scabs issue forth as if the vapors of the gross humors can exit; and cautery site on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered throughout; and it appears manifestly, then it is necessary that you make cauteries with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery in the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and four cauteries on the spine of the back, and one on the chest and another on the side, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the veins that are on the rear calcifying, lest you burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do of cauterizing, the more you do of helping, and it benefits; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cauterization if they sense it like a healthy person, because the body is already almost totally corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manners of the iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing the wound with flour paste mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to a member and is treated with medicines and ointments and plasters, and it is not healthy, then you make cauterizations on the member according to its size and smallness of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep into the skin of the body; then treat with ointments until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And often one performs cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of a nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is removed the inflammation; and in no way does he intervene unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and outlets of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of abscesses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "abscesses" is inflamed, and the engines of medicine are of no value, then one cauteries with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the skin of the heart, until the whiteness is eliminated, and its color is changed; then cure with flour of fenugreek and of lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of almonds, each a part; and mix all together, and bind with a dressing, and apply to the limb until it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a cancer appears at its onset, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that forms a circle, entirely around the tumor.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And wise men say that one should perform cautery at the center of the cancer; and it does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to avoid it; and a more direct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or from the excessive fluid that it makes or from the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, very old) and has little blood, or for their tension; and you see hasten to heal: then cauterize thoroughly with many small cauteries in pricking; afterwards let it be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she hastens to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you perceive the entire fire cautery, heat the cautery to the form it is.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" so that the cauteries penetrate to the heart, and be such the cauteries that the patient feels them deeply in some manner that the course of the purification is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire through iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a mangling of a limb, for it eats away the members just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the patient who can suffer from cautery together with fire, then heat the small and large clavicle cauteries subtly according to what is suitable for the patient or the disease; after cauterizing all parts so that you remove all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything corrupted is eliminated.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and apply to the limbs cauteries suffering from burning with oil until the burns of hot fire are eliminated, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of swollen eyes producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then recommence the cautery on those who remain of the corrupted limbs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this treatment has often been cured by medicine ague in the place of fire cautery; but however fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of medicine ague in the division: take as much as you have need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that our feet are affected by a disease called "clothes" according to our intention, and it is a big faulty thing which affects the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries of this disease are in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the cautery iron as if it were a hollow tube, and make it from good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the nail on all sides, and that it has subtle margins; afterwards put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand totally around the nail until it comes to the font of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot and decay; then make an emplaster of wild savages' herbs boiled with oil, and leave the emplaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be disrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the limb of inflammation by cleaning it so much that it becomes healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by evil humors in the body, and many times it happens in the hands and in the feet, then you must apply warm water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a cane of iron or a pen of wood, and place it on the nail and the heel, that is to say for removing warts; and place the cane thus so it surrounds everything around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and then find the warm water deep into the root; and let the patient suffer a little the biting of the warm water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will deracinate all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Here is the translation:
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble with cold or nerves, or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you do three fire cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one fire cautery between each vertebra; and one fire cautery or foot, and one on the stomach for olive cautery; if they let the trembling, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of painful pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear by default through the body's baths, or pus-filled pustules, that come from gross corrupt materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary first when they appear that one makes cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization of iron of myrtle, from which the point should be taken in fire, or of root of aristologe long, or of lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never cauterize at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow from the inquiry ahead, but are dislodged the superfluous things that come from them, and are healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Here is the translation:
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever it happens to nobody, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it steady as much as the blood is appeased beneath your finger, and no more comes out; then apply fire cautery, olive oil, more or less small and large as it becomes all red; then take .i., great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is routed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery steady until the blood is reestablished.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it happens to burst forth when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stanched; and beware that you do not irritate the nerve that is nearby, and that another malice does not come upon the patient; and know that when blood does not flow from the artery, it cannot be well stanched, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the three methods that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with a thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stanch blood; and so be bound and held firmly afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the stanching of the blood in a narrow place, either by wrapping tightly with cloths or by putting things firmly on, or similar things, does not profit unless it is done promptly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to none and he does not have a better medicine present, then one must put their finger index on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bend well so that it is reset above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but move the soft part of the arm often so that it be very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and reset; and make inquiries beforehand about those who need cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter, all diseases require fire cautery or medicine burning, and the instruments and causes and the forms of cauteries; and I placed that chapter among the chief just below, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method because it is easier to find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin it, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one on cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you do not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who harm themselves with their disease so that they die easily by the abundance of their malady, and by the greatness of their wickedness; and of this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of this there is one who gives his sense, and says: "wait, I am cured"; and the disease is despised.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open foolishly but wisely of that which you are certain, and of that which you can have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your diseases so that health may be converted; and this will aid you to acquire good renown, and glory, and long memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and direction, and may you be willing to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here is the translation:
dou chief plein d’aigue	a full head of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	It is known that this disease often comes from the wet nurse to the infant, and when the nurse holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it happens because of a wrong posture that one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen hasten to death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is better to abandon the work in certain treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew so much every day that it could not be supported; and the moisture was so great that it became mortal, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone under the siphac, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a large incision in the head; and it should be as long as we need, so that the moisture flows; and see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make four incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the signs that you observe the commissures of the chief overtly from each part, and the water flows out when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond to you: then it is necessary to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after cutting, remove all moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the edges of the wound together with drapes and powders, and put in wine and oil, and let it be until the fifth day; then dislodge, and treat the wound by taping and by ointments, and let the head be straightened, and give to the patient dry food free from moisture as much as possible so that the limb may be comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you examine where the abscess opens up, and assemble the water flow; for it is never before, never behind, never to the right, and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Here is the translation:
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or in the breast, and the disease is ancient, and the medical treatment does not benefit at all, then the last resort cure is the cautery with fire that one uses to cauterize the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you cover the wounds, that the patient holds his head back; after he rubs the limb with a rough drape as much as the arteries appear, then straightens the patient's neck to the entire drape; then look where the veins beat, and the lines of the one and the other are behind the ears, and a little are restored; then sign the lines of the notch, then cover the one and the other with a thin spatula of two edges, as much as the vein reaches to the bone, and that is done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the pointed instrument beneath the artery and cauterize above, cutting just as .ij. fingers deep across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then the blood constantly flows out above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark an inch and make a cut just to the bone; and as it is necessary to put blood flowing if it is six ounces, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the replenishment of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains on the bone point of syrup, if it happens that abscesses burst forth, then hold the wound and bind it, and the treatment of ointment until it is healthy.
de emigrainne	of the migrating (or wandering)
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the migrating pain comes, and catarrh agitates, due to the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and old worn-out forehead and similar things, and it is treated by ways of cures of medicine and all that does not profit him, if we extract the arteries from the temples and the cauteries, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs on their temples grow back, and attends to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and is poorly received by those who are too cold; and if it is received, then they strain their neck from certain drapery, then rub the place of a rough cloth, and raise the place of warm water as much as the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula in the form of:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with pincers, and separate well the layers that are beneath each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the uncinate, then cover that part according to the quantity of two inches.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Because she is not cupped, thus she does not jump the blood entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the 6 veins, just up to the 3rd; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you bind it with a double thread of strong silk, which will not allow it to move before the closure of the wound, and allows the flow of blood; then cover the superfluous tissue that is between the 6 ligatures at that hour, and then, if you see, so cauterize with a cautery cutellaire up to the bone as much as the joints are covered; and this is the mother work, if the patient has no fever and it is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish the moisture: because it is of great aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries that one fills the vein with much cotton and places well-made tents; and when you remove them, if they are cured by dry medicines that make the flesh grow, and of tents, until it is healthy; and if without cutting into the artery as soon as you operate, if you hasten to cover with cautery, or you fill the vein with vitriol and hold it in your hand so the blood is stanched; and if you do not have this present, if you put on the vein your finger so the blood congeals, and raise the vein of cold water until the blood stops, and be steady as it is necessary; and what is more moderate and lighter in extracting the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this trenchant cautery of .ij. parts, but the trenchant should be well spaced to avoid burning for too long a time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too hot, they hold less their warmth.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the .ij. small knives .i. a large space, and then when you have signed on the edges of the .ij. veins, and you place the iron rod burning so much that it comes just to the bone, and cover the vein in .ij. veins; and be separated between the .ij. parts because it is not suitable for this cautery from top to bottom; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from veins that are on the top of the forehead, and it does not benefit from a medical treatment that one makes, and you see the face of the patient becoming red, and feel at the front of the walk as if of frenzy; and if they are tense and moist so that the hair of the papers is fallen, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, it has need of this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it "cured contusion", and it is that you make a scratch on the patient who has this disease in the hairs of his forehead, then make three equal incisions according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as two fingers deep into the forehead, descending downwards to the nose, and the others two fingers wide along the edges above the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are two fingers wide above the papers; and keep your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across the joints; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many drapings to suck out the blood, then apply the spatula, well-greased with two parts of that which is its form.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Of the incision that is to be made at the temple just up to the second incision; and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two fissures up to the entire surface that is on the bone, then make another part of the mean incision just up to the other second, and then extract this spatula-like thing.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "scalpel", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is dull, not very sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the scalpel cutting towards the airy flesh at the heart, and the gentle cut towards the bone, and the cut as far as it reaches the middle seam.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision continues until it reaches what opens at the heart, and then afterwards make another cut in the middle seam until the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press the flesh for the taken blood; then put in each seam a swab of old cotton, and apply moistened drapes with wine and oil and vinegar, and beware that apostemes do not come; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and add great abundance of warm water, then the cure of ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other cures which heal wounds, until it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	of the evacuation of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a vein is accustomed to flow with difficulty, and you see the eyes sunken and small, and the vision is cloudy, and the papers are burned; and the hair falls out, and where the head is in pain from an acute disease, and the patient is exhausted; then know by these signs that those matters and this catharsis do not come forth except from many veins, and the cure is more difficult than it is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a large incision in the forehead, and another just as wide nearby.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision just up to the bone; and separate your hand from the edges of the temples that are moving with the hammer; and when the bone is uncovered, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then clean between the two lips of the incision and put in much cotton, and apply tincture of linen; then lay over a dressing soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is open, you must scrub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with excitant things that cause growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take three parties of flour of wheat, and of colocynth three parties, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to excite growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of these things: either grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing as iron; or seed, as if jasmine, beans, peas; or flowing thing as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When the bone grows in the pierced ear or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear, and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, distill some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then perform extraction; and when the discharge is made from the condenser, and the nostrils are stopped up when the discharges come, and place pieces of cloth or wool over the ear; and hold the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes forth through this treatment; and if it does not come forth, then perform extraction with subtle pincers, so that is the method.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, it's good; if not, you perform extraction with a subtle hook of small double curvature; and if it doesn't come out by this, you make a cane of iron and insert the head of the cane into the ear hole strongly, and stop up what is around the cane with wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; then you pull it out in the form, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this manner, you take glue from which you take the bones, and put some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton inside; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever thing it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not succeed in all these things that we have said, hasten to open the ear thus that the abscess bursts, and spasm; and the manner of the opening is that you first make the patient healthy from the cephalic disease, and extract blood according to the measure of its strength, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it depends on fat or flesh; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck hastily into your mouth; and cure until they are healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it inflates, administer an extraction; and if it cannot exit, administer a spatula with a subtle touch according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision into that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, so that you have made many pieces; then extract with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction may be alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where it falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient uses the discharge of condenser first, and fills the ear with much cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be placed on that same ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it gets worse from that point, it's bad.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it doesn't, take many piers according to the length of your thumb and fingers, and heat them a little by fire; and place one or two of them on his ear, and attach it with another pier from another part, and make a layer on top of the pier in the ear; and don't stop doing this from pier to pier until the pain has gone entirely away, and thus it gets entirely better; and if you see, take the joint, and put one of the heads in the ear, and the other head takes fire so that the most tender joint is roasted; then redo another layer of other joints until the pain has gone entirely away, as we have said about the pier.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a thorn and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large-bodied so that one can feel it, then proceed with the gentle extraction of pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where you treat distillations, and the cure does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in sunlight: if no worms appear, then remove them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, take the candle of what is their form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle part of the needle in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck forcefully into the whole vein; do this often until all the veins are seen.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, stop up the vein with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not spring forth as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this entire instrument, because it is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is of silver or copper narrowed below at a small hole, and above opened for distillation; and to press within the distillation with an instrument of well-made copper, and if you see take the scraping and enveloped around the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the candle, and the candle is in the ear; then insert into the scraping all the cotton, and press your hand moderately so that the oil is distilled or extracted from the ear; and the patient feels it within, and it is the distillations which are warmed by fire, so that they are distilled in the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with no holes in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through swelling of a wound, or when a piece of flesh is born inside the ear, and these swellings come many times in front of the ear, if one cannot see it; and many times it happens that the hole becomes small, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes in front, if one cannot see it, is of grievous sanitation in many dispositions, and in this one sees that you must put the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opilation, then the work has achieved all this spatium of which it is the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be smooth and even in front and behind all plain, so that it does not obstruct the ear; if the opilation is of flesh born or growth of the ear, then you hold as pincers subtly, and lift gently, until this growth is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operations are deep in the ear, take a subtle, light razor and heat it slightly by fire, then place it in the course of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstructions that the patient feels great pain in the ear, perceive lightly, and be careful not to disturb the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the size of the perforation, and apply it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not leave it for a day until the wound is dried, or take a tent and apply rose water ointment, and sprinkle vitriol powder; and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another ointmented tent made of rose oil and wax, so that the inflammation is removed; then cure until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, soak an sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the flow of blood which are treating with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papyra (paper-like skin)
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Here is the translation:
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.
