And if they are without decay, the fire cautery is subtle and the cautery practitioner, after incision, values highly; and many times they repair, as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not grow back.
de la gresle	of the scab
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times things come in papers from the eyes that seem big in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "grandine", and it's an accumulation of great moisture above and below; the work is such: take care that the grandine moves from one part to another, and it's a light thing to know; make then the large donation, then scrape each part lightly, then take them as pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, do not hurt the patient at all; and if the crack is large, assemble it into a cast, and cure until it is healthy; and if it is small, do not use force, for the ointments restore it quickly and often.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine descends from the inside of the ear towards the upper part, invert the skin, and grasp the grandine with pincers, and cover and press from one part to another; and if the skin is separated by incision, it does not hurt; and when the grandine is covered, leave the saline water in the oil, and cure the place of what heals the patient's injury as much as possible.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Here is the translation:
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand against your arm and feel the numbness entering within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the surgery is that the patient places their head in your hands; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that each part contains of fatness, then place it on them; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the fatness is gathered within the circle; then make a small incision in the moisture with a sharp scalpel, and let it not be larger than the wound made for a vein opening; and make the skin deep enough until you reach the fatness; and in many dispositions, fatness comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract from there a piece of cloth, charpit between your fingers at the defect, and turn your hand to the right and to the left so that it is spread out; and be careful not to touch the incision, lest you reach the entire scalpel just up to the eye, lest you bloody it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the patient's skin does not open at the beginning of the wound, increase the wound slightly so it opens; then extract as we have said, then wrap in cloths and water, and put on the limb, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break their own arm and put it back to correct the moisture that has gone bad.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the arm, then treat it with soothing ointments until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of papers are born awkwardly other than naturally, and are enveloped, they harm the eyes, and bring about kinds of diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albumen, so much that it is due to the destruction of the eyes; and there is a cure in .iii. ways: either by fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterizing, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your healthy hand, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, thrust a needle through all of it; and let it be beneath the margin of the paper where the hairs grow from those hairs, and pull the thread above all of the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part beneath the paper, beneath the aligned hairs, all of the spatula coping, from the great mirror up to the small; then extract the thread, and put beneath the paper a small piece of cotton and drapery, then sign on the paper a figure of an inch, if like the leaf of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevated on the paper which is divided into sections.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you have a mastery of coping with a great quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened; then shape all the spatula-like instruments on the two lines that you have signed, and start from the great artery just a little; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the heart, then strip it completely; then assemble the two lips with a thread of subtle wool, and suck out the blood, and remove the superfluity of the filaments on the two eyebrows to all sticky things, if you want to do this; and if not, if you have no cure, then leave the thread and filaments until three or four days; then treat the wound without a constraining dressing of dry things, for the paper revives suddenly at the assembly of the wound and its joining, but the dressing is muddling (as the ancients said), and it's work without fear; and if there's another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is like the flower of myrtle, as we have described, to three onions separated according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then apply to those who have small equal forces in harmony with the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the tissues, and the thing is not even, take a needle or thread, and insert it into the figure; and put another thread beside the large artery, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have sutured, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suturing, and cure until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments soothing; but it often happens that the hairs of the papyrus are converted: thus you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the parchment and make it thin according to what I have said, and then make artificial caines by art, and subtle threads as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is; and take .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above what appears on the surface of the eye's parchment, and stretch the .ij. caines of the .ij. parties forcibly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which will be stretched more and more and will putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if the wound resists to some forces, then cure until it is healthy; and when the wound has been sewn, and if the papyrus has been lifted, and the hairs will no longer sprout; and this is the form of the two canals that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you take a subtle needle, and thread .i. fine and subtle silk thread; then assemble the heads and tie one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the hunt .i. another subtle silk thread briefly, and tie the two ends of the thread; then put the patient's head in your healthy hand; and let it dry in the sun so that the operation is clear, for this is a subtle and minor operation, then put the needle at the root of the hair implanted, and make it pierce through the skin hastily until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the hunt, and put into the hunt that hair, if there are .i. or .ij. or .iij. or more; then pull out your hand as much as the hairs come forth at the root of the hair implanted with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then draw the hunt to the bottom of all the thread that you had arranged, so that the hunt comes forth through the hole above and that you see it by the vision of the eye; then if you draw the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and let it stay closed .ij. hours or .iij., until the hair is rooted in its place and grows the flesh on top; and if the hairs are small, then accompany .i. long hair of natural whiskers, and raise it with that which you leave, so that it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purification of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the porridge comes into the eye, it has two manners: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a blow, or from a cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you split open the wound, and separate its lips, and put in threads of linen, and bind it so it may be healthy; and it does not seem that you should use in its cure things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease returns worse than before; but work with things that soften, such as fenugreic; and rose water or plantain and linseed oil are cooked, and ointments of dyaquilon founded in one of the eyes, and envelop a bandage, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of this treatment is that you take heed not to let it settle back into its former shape; and these workings that we have spoken of are only adjournments of this disease, so it does not relapse into its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is disfigured, truly named "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of working on it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and fix it in the flesh, and make a perforation from the left arm up to the right, so that the threads go into the head of the flesh; then stretch the flesh over the entire needle, and cover with a large spatulum.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the papyrus returns to its former shape, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the papyrus, and make two cuts or seams within the papyrus; and be the heads of the two cuts at the angles of the incision that you have covered, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as good as the figure of a letter that has no "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are affected, from what follows the papyrus, then adjust the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure it with the medicines we have spoken of, and apply poultices, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from fissure or cutting or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain fissure beneath the hairs of the papyrus, and according to what is before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know how to make the figure return to its natural form; and the same patients, according to what they need of operation and of strengthening in more disposals.
dou soudement de la papiere	because of the burning of the parchment
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this burning has affected men in such a way that the parchment above is burnt with the white of the oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to apply the point of a razor beneath the parchment, and lift it high; and hold as pincers, until you grasp what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot suffer from the spatula being too sharp or scratching the oil; and make your incision, where you carefully remove the assembled tissue, gently, so that the parchment regains its natural form; and it is entirely healthy, and never again becomes inflamed or irritated, and raises a gentle and soothing warmth, and of collyrium; then place between the parchment and the oil a layer of linen, and put on the oil a soft and abundant dressing; and after three days use a soothing collyrium and similar things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the corner of the eye is in two ways: it is nervous and appears like a hard, dry crust, and another which is not nervous, but appears as a white, congealed moisture, which when touched with iron and pressed with pincers, cannot be moved; and one and the other appearance begins to turn towards the great artery, and grows little by little until it covers all sight and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts their head in a healthy position, then they open their eyes; and he takes the skin with his hand, then curves the finger like small pincers, and holds it above; then take a needle, and I put horsehair or cow hair or beef thread on it, strong and firm; and double the point of the needle a little and fix it in the finger, and pass it through the entire needle, and hold the finger with a thread and hold it above, and remove all the hair from the side of the finger which touches the skin and the vein just to the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the artery, subtle and with small forces, and let the natural skin or artery, so that by incision does not disturb the course of the veins accustomed; and never does the finger get stuck on the nail solely, and on the thread, as we have said; then remove all the skin subtly, which is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the artery does not touch the raw skin and break it, and that the vein is not perceived; and after the incision, pour a little warm broth into the oil, and make a collar of litargyrum, and leave it until the next day; then cure what needs to be cured as much as it can be healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the finger is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the veins cannot enter, many times this type of finger is cured with medicines; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see the cover, then open the oil from the patient, and take the subtle artery slightly according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the finger subtly, and if you see that it diminishes at all and the reason presses on, then distill from your mouth into the collier made of litargy and two red collars and brocade, and stop the eye just until the next day; then restart the other treatment according to this same work, as long as it is completely exhausted.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to the eye, then as an aposteme heats up, then milk it, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healthy, then restart the treatment as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh shows great harm in the eye during the night, then suspend it on the ninth [note: probably a mistake, should be "oncle" meaning uncle or ninth is not clear], and cut off a part but not entirely, so that the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the red collier made of litargy.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Here is the translation:
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But always it is necessary that you adjust the treatment according to the natural weakness of each eye; and the accidental way, in work with iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	from the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are veins that are red and covered on the eye, and take away its function and obscure the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary then at first that you examine the eye, in which the veins are, it is strong, and there is no other disease besides the vein; therefore, take care in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head in a healthy position, then support those veins all around according to their wisdom, and let the veins be subtle and double according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be an eleven-inch incision by degrees in this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you coil the subtle forces of those veins skillfully, and suck out the blood hour after hour, until you see that you remove those veins from the eye; and beware that you do not block the eye at the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not grasp more than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what is morbidly swollen.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot coil all that in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and is free from hot abscesses, then resume according to this method which is presented before, so that it may be healthy; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Here is the translation:
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, you will see the decay and blackness, if it returns to its entire instrument of which it is the form; and it is called "asper chief", and it was made from iron into a .i. chief reont, and it should be pointed like a lime as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two [hands], and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicines having excitative properties.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the eyes are cloudy, and there is no birth, and the body of the bowel is cloudy, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not renew and is not apostematous, and bad accidents come, know that it is healthy; if not, if there is another engine than to bring back the fistula to the perforated nose according to this form: and it is that you discover the bone through the second time by iron, and by bitter medicines, and when it is discovered thus take the forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and the rod be attenuated up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the patient's arm where the messenger vein is, and hold your hand on the eye of the small finger, then turn until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it through that which comes in if they hold their hand on their nose; and then restore the arm with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and endures the abscesses, then one sees the matter at the nose; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open everywhere, and there is no disturbance in the nose, nor diminishment, then it is necessary to lift the patient; then the healthy one, then apply poultices or ointments without piercing to suck, then put on the eye .i. make a mixture of vinegar and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then hold the eye steady, and bind with bandages and drapels; and the way of the drapels is that you take very soft ones, and double each in three, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity the eyes need; then hold it firmly with a strong bandage, and reapply the poultices to suck without piercing; then remove the poultices and let the eye be steady day and night, and if it becomes weak, then it is necessary to strengthen it more; then remove the binding after a day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that's good; if not; then reapply the bandage and drapels and the poultices until it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	because of the tearing of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woven fabric, then open, and comes from papers as if .i. grains of resins, and it is astonishing to see; then if you see the weaving, the works are such that you put a needle in the root of the part below up to the one above, then put another needle where there is .i. double thread of the part of the armier; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cover the eye with double thread and tie a part of the weave around, and hold it well, then remove the needle and put on the eye again moistened with abundant use; and let it be until the threads are joined with the weave, then heal the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healthy; and no time the wound is held back by the weave each part of a circle of drap, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes take on a great appearance, if they perceive in the subtle spatula which comes from the front of the eye, and corrects the moist albuginea and descends into the eyes, and inserts itself thus; then it will be straight until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the hollow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not more than a swelling that forms in the eye, appearing as a descending water, and it is not really water; and the manner of its appearance is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take the head between your hands from both parts, and move it so that you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then be still and do not descend or disperse the light, and see if the patient sees things as they should; and if they do not descry below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
des aigues de l’oil	from the corners of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of the aiguilles in the division, and this is what is necessary to pierce; if one works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye steady and strongly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a hair in that corner of the eye at the part of the least eyelid, then insert the instrument called "almagda" carefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the corner of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the prunele up to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; if you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the woven fabric, and then place the instrument just where the aiguille is, then press it down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Here is the translation:
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest, the patient rises with the second path, puts the fire with the instrument, and when it is thus fixed and does not rise, gently extract the alumga in turning your hand little by little; and then puts back into the water a little of the gemstone, and removes from that eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then puts by default the eyes stupefied or clouded with rose oil and in abundance of egg whites, and mixes it with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on common broth with an abundance of egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which is the form.
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctive slightly, and do not go too deeply in fear, but make it subtle, then pour alumga, as we have said; and at the completion of the work appearing to the patient, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be aware of all movements, and take light food, and does not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and make him see certain things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate this, because the water rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Here is the translation:
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he gets up slowly from his bed, and turns back to his affairs; and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the land of Yrach, who told us that in his country they made an almond piercer, to which one sucked the water, but I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of amputation, because those who do not know them go astray; and they should be properly prepared.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of the bone in this subtle precision, and the last one at three angles aigu.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No time does birth or various kinds of snakes appear, because there are some that resemble scorptions with many feet; and if there is such a snake with an enhanced dark-colored skin, and if it has a snake with a soft bone-colored skin.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of the snakes that are soft and not enhanced, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, and throw the onion at those snakes, and treat them with fire; because it seems that you can sustain the subtle spatula on one side, as long as you know that the snake is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open everything, i.e., the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without mounting above, or abscess appears, drain it as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten to cauterize until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is burned, then throw away or anoint with oil or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the snake does not open, and moisture comes up to the palace, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a new snake in the upper bone, which the struments do not come to cut: then you must put the thread of linen a little thick, and be careful with our hands, and have between each nail of space I or less; and place the patient's head at the end of the thread in his nose as much as possible, and treat it with odorant until it comes out through the nose within the mouth; and many times children do so at school, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after another in being as we are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the nails have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the filament, suck out the blood, and mix the filament in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put on the nose a poultice of plantain for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, where they distill oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or copper, resembling a covered lamp, like a tube, and the conduits are thus; and if you see, make a closed tube, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have .i. a handle on the head to hold it while one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease occurs on the skin above the nose which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large soon, so it is visible to behold; and for this reason you must take measures at the beginning, and remove everything far, then put above the skin the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in applying until it be large, take heed if it is hard, of fixed color, of poor sensation: if you do not touch with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when one applies it many times, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of fixed color, and you see that one can completely remove, then beware of the patient and remove their fear, and cure the skin of dry and withering things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is affected and ulcerated
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when continuous solutions come into one of these cartilaginous openings, it profits little, because in some homes.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to chant when it has come to none, if you see that the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then join the two lips to a suture, and cure until it is healthy; and if the lips are somewhat separated from one part and another, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their skin until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a suture, and hold them in place, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and incense broiled; and put on the powders a piece of strong or other soothing plaster, and let it adhere by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the cost is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the cost of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of men who have dense abscesses on their lips, similar to grains of vetch, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each knot, and take them with pincers and cut in each part; then apply the oil after the incision of vitriol burnt, so that the wound may be stained; and then apply the oil of iris, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the decay of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the gums are inflamed where they are attached, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary that you support them with bandages, and apply a remedy to their root, and let the blood or sap flow; then put on the vitriol broth, or other powders that restrain and dry; and if that gum returns after the incision, and many times happens, if you apply the remedy a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for coping.
des sordens	Of the abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, deep in the mouth between the gums, scabs that are black and bitter and green, as long as the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth are putrid; if it is necessary that you take the patient's head between your hands, and their jaw should be steady, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, so that nothing remains; and thus make a remedy for blackness and greenness and jaundice and other taints, so that they are cured; and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good; if not, then restart on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth have need of various forms of instruments for extraction, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots that one extracts from the teeth have other forms than those that one extracts between the teeth; and these forms and others should be well-equipped with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay doing so for as long as you can, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very delicate substance up to the point where one has no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to receive treatment, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and makes them treat the good tooth; and nonetheless the pain does not depart from there, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have already wanted to do this to those who are healthy; and when you are well certain of the hurting tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula strongly to ward off the gum on all parts; then you take it in your two fingers or subtle pincers at the first little by little, as long as it is well loosened, then you hold it firmly with the pincers; and so the head of the patient remains still between your knees, and you hold it well so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part lightly, and you remove it just like you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are perceived and gnashed, it is necessary that you fill them with drapels, there where the perforations are; and if you hold subtly as with tongs, so they do not break while holding; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you do well to beware that you do not break it, and leave a part remaining, and reveal to the patient by the wickedness of the root more great pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, in their haste and hardness, often break the cartilage, and do not amend what we have recounted; but they come to be treated for that great illness caused by the roots that remain, or for the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, if you wash with wine or vinegar and sage; and if blood comes out, which often happens, apply the vitriol ointment; and if it does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	Here is the translation:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs so they do not bend in the traction, and let them be of iron well-made, and let them be toothed to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the thigh remains in the stretcher, it is necessary that you put a cotton cloth moistened with warm water on it for two days or more.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the limbs are softened, then apply the clamps called "algefri", which make the head seem like a beak of a bird; and thus they are made similar to a file and that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue from all these pincers, then it is necessary that you discover the flesh entirely surrounding the root, and he puts on the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a palate scraper, from which this is their form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this, it is good; if not, then you help with all the instruments, from which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has several grooves, from which the form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front of the dens' ratio, and of this instrument that resembles large pincers, from which the form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And it should be these instruments strong so that they cannot break, and know that many of the dens' instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtly find by themselves their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are certain diseases where the ancients did not teach at all about the diversity of instruments; and it breaks no cartilage or bone, or it corrupts, if one searches for these instruments that it needs, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not slip away, but can hold and support; and then restore the limb with suitable medicines, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the natural body, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, if it needs to be known that the teeth are not after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot straighten or file: then take the root; and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument which has a similar shape, and is like a small iron hook bent into a point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping is little by little in the morning hours for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file with a similar file as its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file of which one makes the needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in the morning hours lightly, so that it does not move until it settles; then the plane at the end has no roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, if it needs to be filed to be even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth are dislodged, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on them so they do not eat, and you treat them with constricting medicines, but it is of no value; if you need to restrain them with a thread of gold, because the silver thread turns green and rotten, but the gold does not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you want to adjust the teeth, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the teeth among the bad ones, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then recommence the covering up to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and steadily, so they do not move at all; and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the heads of the thread to a tin, and assemble them, and put them back between the healthy tooth, and set it so it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it thus tightened as much as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the threads break, hold it with another thread; if it stays in place and serves thus all its time, and this is the way of the teeth and the shape of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and the two molar teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said; and do not intervene with those who are not skilled and suffer, and never make the shape of a tooth like an ivory tusk, and put it in the place where the defect is, and hold it in place as we have said, and let it stay and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	It never happens that the threads which come from under the tongue or nature, do not stay thus; or by accident of a wounded mouth; and the works are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue; then take the nervous thread of the large size, so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is hardness or numbness, and it is suddenly wounded, thrust the uncinate and take the large ligament; and beware that the fissure is not too deep in the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift the water of rose and of hazel, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a tincture of linen; and apply it to the patient each night, so that their jaws cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the flow of blood comes, apply a glassy vitriol ointment on the spot; and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with a slow cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see that the color is dark or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a cancer; and if it declines to a bluish color, and there is moisture, apply the onychine, and make a subtle spatula-like instrument, and deliver one part and another; and if the wound does not heal with your operation, apply vitriol ointment until it is stained, then return to your operation until you treat everything completely; then lift the water of hazel and of seed, and cure with other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a swelling comes in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called II ulcers, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, take care: if it is an abscess with little sense and a faulty color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.
