And one must thus put this ventouse on the limb: take the clamp of wax or linen, and place it in the ventouse across the verge that is in the ventouse, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the ventouse so it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and these two are on the perforation as we have said, so that when one wants to, the vapor goes out, and one removes the ventouse; and take the linen as before, and reapply it frequently, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping which is administered in disease of pleurisy, to all acute, there is no verge nor pertus, and it's not administered unless when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only sufficiently; and that's the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés. Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish mirrors themselves of this chapter, which they did not find in any of the ancient books, nor did they read a letter about it; and for this reason is strange the science in our land, because I did not find any good in it; and I know nothing, except through the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the experience of my life; and I have described to you here in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and clearly demonstrated the forms of instruments that are necessary, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where wisdom puts its understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who have experienced it know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breakage or dislocation or twisting or bruising occurs somewhere, it is necessary to hasten the healing of the patient on one side and the other, so that nothing stops you completely, whether from weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age; or if the tendons are not very strong, or too cold; and avoid cold joints, that is to say frozen joints, and the flesh of birds and of goats, and do not drink any wine, and do not eat dry and lean meat, and do not fill oneself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, so that you have no doubt of hot abscess, nor of spreading of matter in the limb; if the patient returns to his first government that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or it has viscosity, just as fermenting in water, and rice, and bread, and feet, and pork belly, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a suitable nourishment represents marrow and more quickly heals the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well rejoined or reunited according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, as in the case of small children; but there is no cure, reset the broken bone with a large tendon that has been separated and join the limb together, so that it becomes strong as it was before; and do not stop them from their work, and for this reason they need to be nourished with coarse food, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a break that goes to the arvolt, and another in agitating, as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it breaks with a wound, and breaks all along a small crack.

And in each manner he has his engine, and his proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings back to its place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs because the joints are twisted, and appear well by palpation, and sound when pressing with the hand; and when there is no tortuosity in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no point of fracture; but he can have tortuosity, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move the hand, but put on medications that come hereafter, and then hold steady now subtly.

And know that the fracture that goes into the arvol, and are the two disjointed parts, they must now be put in equal alignment, so that abscesses do not come to life; and if abscesses come, let them wait for a day, until the abscesses are appeased; then put it in the same place where you can lift and guide, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restorations of that which has pieces; then hold steady, as it is necessary after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone in the joint is broken, whether it's a part of two bones, or a hand or foot, or a small limb, or a cord, or a cord and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are dislocated, you reset them by all means in their proper place, as much as you can, and take care not to cause further injury or pain to the patient through your work; and adjust the two heads of the bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: if you straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as they do who come through their work of abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.

Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.

Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the course is broken, I will tell you the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not suit to tighten these stars all at once on the broken limbs the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plasterer restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take abrasives and ladanium and enula and asa fetida and Arabic gum and myrrh, in this proportion .x. 3.; mirre and aloe, in this proportion .v. 3.; and alechil .viiij. 3.; and make into powder, and mix with abundant egg white; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores the broken bones, and is suitable for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to apply a plaster that is worth twisting: take mugwort and violets, at X marks; mix and grind, at VIII marks; add acaice VI marks; boil Armenian bole in X marks, and crush well, and concoct with water or abundance of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to apply a plaster to joints and relieve them of their dislocations, and appease the sudden pain, and the size of the bone, and the breakage: take new flax, and grind it in oil and cooked oil, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore at all, but they are good for appeasing hot abscesses, and properly alleviating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to restore broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earthy peony leaves, crush them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to apply a plaster for the restoration of bone fracture and to diminish the remainder of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat more forcefully than the first, when a stubborn abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and seeds of lin, balauste, mellilote, and sansuce, and flowers of violets and camomile, of all one part; and crush, and mix with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except for cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one should apply to the broken member, to restore, things which are a little warm, like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of applying that is good for a lesion and pain: take mugwort and chamomile decotions, or pellets of bird's foot, and vismallave, and make it even, and crush them, and make an application on the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone out of its place; if you do not loosen it for many days. And if pain comes to the limb, or pruritis, without rest or inflammation, hasten, and loosen, and remove the dressing now; and take a lighter bandage, and a sponge with seawater, and dip in water, and lift up the limb, until the pruritis ceases, and the pain is appeased. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry, moistened linen cloth, or oil of rose, and bind it with a nut, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle treatment, and a little dressing, and do not constrict it too strongly as before; and continue subtly until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you have mastered the poultice and the bandage, then resume it, as you did previously in equal measure.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb in accordance with what we have said, do not disjoin it further than after three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the bruise becomes apparent, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh on the bone; then restrain more than before, and the limb will fatten, as I said previously; and if you see that the limb dries up more than needed, know that nourishment cannot come; therefore bring an infusion of warm water every time you disjoin it, and let it be every third day, and ease the limb a little; by this work, then, the nourishment comes to the limb, and quickly mends what the foolish doctor has made worse: it is bad, and if these are poor works, and I do not see anything else but to leave it alone and open it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures and diverse figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are fractures that are made by percussion of a sword, and the neck bone breaks all the way to the spine which is beneath the bone, just as if it were shattered or crushed; and therefore this kind of fracture is called "shattering".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the spear strikes the bone from above, piercing senselessly, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two grand or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a buried percussion, or fissure or break of the neck of the stone, or fall on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating wound that approaches just below the skin which is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this is the wound whether large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is repeated in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the crack is small, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound that is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone enter downwards, and the bone is hollowed out as when the caster casts into the molds; if they cast within the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have damp or moist bones, like the head of a child; and it has all these kinds of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like that; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all ways of breaking by the withdrawal from them, and the inquiry into tendons, and by the corrupted flesh that is on.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of the hair-like [structure] is known by that when one has uncovered the bone, and one rubs against it, then the black breaking opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of breaking, beware of accidents that harm the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and numbness, and feverish ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in various dispositions, lest it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an immediate accident, and you expect a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nave comes first to you, and it is in winter, then you must open the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to open the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone reaches just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the affected part in this way: and it is necessary that you take hold of the chief nerve of the ailing patient, and uncover it on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more softly than you can, and if the flow of blood comes to uncover the bone, or abscess forms, then the aid of what is necessary, and it is necessary that you fill the place with poulticed moilliez oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess is appeased, and be assured of the flow of blood; then begin to ostentate on the bone, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut straight beforehand, and it is the form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then you make another stitching even larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of diverse stitches, some tight and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are of iron indeed; and in working lightly, so that you do not blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you make a perforation around it, so that you administer moderate blows with a hammer, not too deeply so that they do not penetrate beyond the bone of the test, and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have more, if each one returns to its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have blows for all tests; and this is the form of the three manners of blows.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of blows to pierce into the broken bone is that you put a blow on the bone, and turn your fingers so that you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the blow in another place a little afterwards, and do it all around, then make incisions in the space of the bone which is between the breaks, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you hold as if with pincers; and beware that you do not touch the brain or the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone, and drawn it out, then it is necessary that you remove the excess flesh which remains on the bone to all the other instruments similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more delicate and subtle than the other incisors; and if there remain none of the small bones, or no scales, then they lightly adhere to one of the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of surgery is what Galen said, which is more wise; and he praised it greatly, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where the break appears, so that when you have discovered that part, then put beneath the head of this lenticular incision the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the affected area is on the other side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then make a small incision above, so that you lightly touch the entire bone around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath; if it is attached to the bone, lift it lightly, for they are well aware of the harm, and feel fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is covered only superficially above, and there are small pieces, so it is necessary to remove that asperity, and to extract the scales with a subtle rasping tool which you must have in various quantities, to prepare each place most conveniently, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rasp before with large rasping tools, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease from doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate hair-like fractures and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you prepare the cause according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily responded to by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is deep, it is necessary that you apply a dressing of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another doubled dressing, either two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first dressing; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not irritate the wound, then apply another layer above, and do not strain too much, until the wound is somewhat consoled; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscesses are pacified, then remove them, and administer medicines such as roots of plants, flour of seeds, powder of incense, and aristologist, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer gentle medicines without biting; and be careful that the wound is not too open, so that you do not leave the opening, nor allow it to assemble a scab, for when a scab assembles on the membrane of the brain, it corrodes and becomes putrid, and brings great harm to the patient; for when you apply something biting on the wound, it irritates above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Here is the translation:
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no fire that comes from the medicine that one has applied, which has such a virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue them together in a dressing; then apply the cure in various ways as needed, until it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that no time are broken the three parts of the nail above, or one part by the solvent, for they are three bones; and this below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it does not make force to enwrap or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you put your little finger or thumb into the nostril, and insert the breakage into your finger index, and by gentle pressure, until the nose regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nail, and cannot come out at the joint, then it is necessary that you put it evenly on top of a straight rod a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the breakage is of two parts, do it in another way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscesses that have swollen are appeased, then put on the head of the nose tentatively with drapings of linen, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you apply it on one side, the break is there; and let the tendons be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that one must moisten the tents in mud, and move each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that it is good, but rather they should be moistened with a concoction of egg white and powder of mill; then leave the tents, until the bones are firm, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes apply it on the nose where the tendons of the egg are, and if there is a swollen drapery within, and it holds the break, and soothes the patient among; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are operating, if you meet cerotate or cotton mollified in rose oil, or in a little pouch of dyacolon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if apostemes (abscesses) come, apply a plaster made of flour of sisament and powder of incense, mixed with egg white, then put on light bandages, and do not tie them too tightly; and if the break in the nose is small, and it is broken into little pieces, extract the fragments comfortably to that, then sew up the fissure, and cure the things that are painful and bitter, and soothe, as with plasters and ointments comfortable to that; and if there is no inner wound in the nose, apply the cure of tents, and put on compresses of lead, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated downwards, and there is no wound in front, and the break is downwards only slightly, and it is not broken in two, because of the corralling within, if one examines it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left jaw, then put your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the break into place, and hold it with the other hand from the front, and set it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is dislocated upwards, then it is necessary that you apply extension to the upper part, so much that it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are moved out of place, or broken, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put it on the broken jawbone, and put on a double dressing; and put on the dressing a well-made steel staple, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so disengage it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and apply a poultice there, made from flour of the mill with plenty of egg or meal of sifted [flour], after you have removed the crust; and put a light poultice there, and if the poultices are effective, and the condition of the patient does not change, let it be until it is healthy; many times it is healthy in eight days.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses or wounds come, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, remove the useless piece of bone that is in the way; if you subtly remove the obstructing fragments with care.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is constricted, then enlarge it with a flame according to the necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have gathered all these pieces, and it does not remain there, if the wound is large, and put on it suitable dressings to cauterize the flesh, so that it be healthy.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks more often beforehand, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners: either it is broken and disarticulated in two, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore; or it has a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken strength; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the break in your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have mastery of extending further, then put under the shoulder on the patient a round sphere of cloth or of wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity; and stretch and lift the strength, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you put the break in place, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot straighten the head of the fracture at the defect, because it comes in deeply, then it is necessary that the patient leans on his shoulder, and puts the espaulier behind, and pushes the ministers below the shoulder, so that the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then adjust the fracture with your fingers, and if you feel debris there, it is necessary that you probe inside; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, apply one of the instruments you have; but put the instrument under the fracture, to ward off the blood flow:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems a spoon, and is not a chess, and be as large as the hollow of the bone and the power of the veins; and have II heads, if you see, and one is large and the other narrow, as is the routing of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, cut into the wound, and if the routing is small, or you doubt hot abscess, fill the wound with drapnels and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come, thus much. It drizzles into rosated oil and in vinegar and in wine, and puts on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The straightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without bandages, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powdered millstone and egg white, and lightly place them on, and put a splint underneath, so you have mastery over it; then take a very large bandage of one palm's width, then put I double-layered dressing on top, and the plaster; then take a subtle steel instrument of three fingers' width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so the head of the bandage is hanging; and put the steel instrument on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and underneath the healthy joint, and underneath the diseased joint; and reset each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the steel instrument does not move above the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligatures loosen, restrain it; and make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow underneath the joint to lift the shoulder high; so alleviate the bruise of the arm by alleviating the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not let bad accidents occur, for up to twenty days; then recommence the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and restrain and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and less than any other remedy.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Here is the translation:
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes beforehand, and not below the heart, if it befalls thus, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the force to appease the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes broken in a thousand ways, but this happens rarely; however, it breaks often at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, it declines to the bottom, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks agility, and all, and by chance vomiting blood, and opens the fractures in the broken bone, and then senses are well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient places himself thus on his back, and you place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of the broken bones with your hands, and subtly put them in order in all the ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put on emplaustres and stoups above the subtle layer of salt, or another lighter dressing, and envelop it in a drapery, and tie it on the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the round ligament to the back, and hold it firmly, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it becomes dislocated, then restrain it; and if you see it becoming loose, due to corrosion or pruritus that comes from the wetness, or pain or abscess, hurry, and take away the dressing, and address what has come in ways of cures; then restore the dressing, and hold it firmly until it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the breakage of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the breakage of the ribs does not occur unless in the large ones behind the back, and at the inner part of the head, and they do not feel it unless because they are slippery; and one feels it well during the interrogation of the two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the resettings are that you make equal the fracture, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a stick, if you have mastery of it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breakage of the ribs declines inward, the patient feels very great pain, and numbness, just like a pierced lung, because the bone pierces the membrane; and it produces spotty ulcers, and all sorts of plant-like growths of blood, and it is a grievous wound, and the old ones have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that they need to administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to cure the rupture by filling the void.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, for hot abscesses will not come, if it has not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has arrived, then bleed it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that no one puts ventouses on the limb, to suck out the matter, and it seems like a reasonable thing; however, there is doubt that the ventouse does not attract the excess humors from the limb due to the weakness of its disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one must cover the limb of a injured thigh with hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equalize the air inside, then one is cured of the treatment for pleurisy, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear through the bone that touches the fabric, and doubt is in the patient, then it is fitting to bend over the broken rib, and it is fitting to put the instrument beneath to ward off the blood flow; and then one must cut into the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure with plasters, until they are healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, then put millstone oil on the affected area, and apply it to the limb; and treat meanwhile the limb of what it needs to abscess, and let it be bandaged tightly on the side where it should be, until it is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	of the breakage of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a breakage comes to the bone of the neck, and soon it will swell; and also it has a swelling on the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, then take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortally wounded in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when one touches them and presses, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient's illness is cured, so one has put a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, then take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and on the back there is a lack of wind and involuntary excretion; and when one has touched it on their belly, if there is an involuntary excretion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is swooning on his back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: do not labor in vain in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the thing most lightweight.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is a hot abscess, put on the spine oil of rose or oil of Mayeu's water, as much as it may be appeased; then put on one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind with a string, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is dislocated, it must be covered on the heart; and remove the bone, then assemble the .ij. lips of the wound, so it is large, at a costure, then the treatment of ointment by making a dressing, as long as it is healthy; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the kowe", you put your pouchet in your left hand, and place it equally with your right hand on your power, then apply the emplastrum and stel on top, if you have mastery; then hold steady, and if there is a dislocated bone, make it straight, and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Because the bone of the hip is broken, and if it breaks, then there is a small amount of diminution at the head; and make a long bandage, and apply it to the paralyzed parts, and come to the patient's pain in the loin, and puncture, and inflame what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand on top, as long as you are above the fracture; and know what kind of break it is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then place equally on that break, so that it may be in a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is very long, or it declines inwardly, then make the patient sit on their belly, until the restoration of that fracture is apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, put a splint on it, then put it in a wooden or wax mold, and hold the fracture steady so it does not move; and apply the remedy under the ribs, until the ligature is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come, do not touch them, until the abscesses are calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it steady as it is fitting, so that there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulders are what is between the neck and the head of the shoulder blade, and if it is fractured, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a full flat plate of moderate thickness, in this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And place the two shoulders thus, and bend them upwards, and sit the patient on his seat; then he throws his broken arm on the plate, until it comes to the joint, and has in the middle a curve of wood, then bends over something heavy or the ministers extend downwards; then put the mirrors with the fracture evenly in their hands together, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his haughtiness, and ties the hand to his neck, then instructs the ministers that one should hold what is on the fracture with their hands, and the others should hold underneath all the ligaments, and each extends to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, hold the bandage below the break, and on the break, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put the bandage meanly below the joint, and another towards the side, below the break; and also if the break is on the side, it is necessary to put the bandage lightly, without labor, until the break is even on the limb, and on the side; then put the break even, as it is necessary, and hold steady, lest an abscess forms, which comes from it.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if apostemes (abscesses) come, do not restrain it less than eight days, and put a soft cloth in oil and rose water, so that the abscesses are appeased; then hold it steady, and the manner of holding it steady is to place the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm at the joint, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the dressing, and hold steady at the joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, and nothing disturbs it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put on the break a larger and stronger splint than the others, and have two fingers' width of space between each splint, and let each splint be as large as it passes over the break; then hold steady with the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter, stronger and less aloof.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the alignment of the stars, and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, if you leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each of three days, so that the bandage does not become inflamed or come loose on the limb, lest the norrissemens cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you add, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, do not undo the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and put their hands on their stomach; and place under the shoulder a plain cushion of equal thickness, and look at each hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken limb does not move, nor are the bonds loosened; if you add by the power of medicine, and give the food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is of prime quality; and when it begins to recover, let it be substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be treated for 40 days in all; and then one must disengage and administer baths and medicines of ointments to repair the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is lazy and swollen, it delays disengaging for 10 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small, and it is the one that follows the pouchet; and the other is large, and it is the one that is beneath, towards the little finger; sometimes the large foscile breaks solely, or the small one, and sometimes they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fractures are broken, the restorations are light, and the healings; and when the large ones are broken, then the healings are bad, and worse than when they are broken and reunited.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's a small fracture that's only slightly broken, then you must extend it lightly, and set it evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's a large fracture, then you must stretch it more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the ministrations as an arm to the part below his hand, or to the linen, and another ministration to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts his eyes equal, according to their better shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage it falls to pieces, set each one in its place, and if there is no disarrangement that grips the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint and bind with a bandage, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breakage it is a wound, I have spoken of it to the singular chapter; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And at the beginning of the restoration, if abscesses or wounds occur, so glaze I apply a dressing made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and I apply the dressing subtly, until the abscesses or wounds are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax, and I put on a plaster made of powdered millet with plenty of egg white, then place the staves, and let the stave of the fracture be stronger and a little larger than the others; and know that it must have six staves or arms in more dispositions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and hold more steady over the fracture than other parts, and always less in aligning, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the dressings that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, from which it is strained, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rewind the limb and the ligament after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, as if a bruise comes to the limb, it is necessary that you warm the limb with hot water, so that the bruises are calmed down; and let the limb not be tightly restrained.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the strapping, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones disjointed, and similar things, adjust them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take a warm poultice that the numbness cannot come to the limb, because it is too constricted, then it is necessary that you soften it a little, and let it stay there for some hours, until the numbness is corrected, and then hold it steady.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not undo the dressing for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	where the patient lies on their back, then they put their hands around their neck, and let their neck be even, and beware of movement and degeneration, and sleep on their back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 days or in 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have two fingers, there have been few fractures, and it does not come but rather frequent dislocations.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or sprained, it is necessary that the patient sits crossed, and sits straight in front of him equally; then he puts his hand on the extended toe, and extends the minister's broken bones, and sets them equal with the mirrors, until they are well joined; and he applies the plaster and the poultices, so that apostemes do not come, then he puts a staple according to the quantity of the blood; and it is enveloped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the middle of the hand near the belly of the palm, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken palm; and then strap it with a long bandage, and let the staple be of soft, smooth skin, as big as the palm of the hand, and strap it, so that it is as necessary.
